4. Set up **FoxyProxy** to use:
   - **SOCKS5 Proxy**: `127.0.0.1`
   - **Port**: `9150`
5. **Activate it only when needed**.

---

### **‚ö† Why Your Current Setup is Risky**
- **Forces ALL Windows traffic through Tor**, not just Brave.
- **Some apps don‚Äôt support SOCKS proxies properly**, leaking your real IP.
- **Tor is not designed for full system routing**, unless you‚Äôre using something like **Tails OS**.

If you‚Äôre just browsing the dark web or trying to be private, **use Brave‚Äôs built-in Tor window**. If you need a **stronger** setup, consider using **Tails OS or a dedicated Tor VPN**.


1. **Test Different USB Ports**:
   - If you‚Äôre using a **wireless dongle**, plug it into a **USB 2.0 port** (black one, not blue).
   - Avoid using ports **near USB 3.0 devices** (they interfere with 2.4GHz).

#### **1. Grant Google Photos Full Storage Access**
1. Open **Settings** on your phone.
2. Navigate to **Apps & notifications** (or just **Apps**).

2. Navigate to:
   ```
   /storage/emulated/128/WhatsApp/Media/WhatsAppVoda Images/
   ```
3. Delete images from there.

Okay, here's my problem and I think it's always been my problem and this is why I've never managed to get it fixed. I cannot navigate to storage/emulated/128/WhatsApp/media.

ChatGPT

Ah, now we‚Äôre getting to the real issue‚Äî**you can‚Äôt navigate to `/storage/emulated/128/WhatsApp/Media/` in any file manager**. That makes sense because **Android restricts access to certain storage locations, especially for Twin Apps**. 

---

### **What‚Äôs Happening?**
- **Android Scoped Storage** hides certain **"isolated storage" paths** (like the one used by Twin Apps).
- File managers, including X-Folder and Files by Google, may not show **Twin App storage** because it‚Äôs treated as a separate user profile.
- **Google Photos can't see or manage those files**, even though they appear in your gallery.

---

## **How to Fix This**
We need a way to **access** the hidden `/storage/emulated/128/` directory.

---

### **Option 1: Check for "Private Storage" in X-Folder**
1. Open **X-Folder**.
2. Navigate to **Internal Storage**.
3. Look for a folder named **Android > Data** (sometimes it‚Äôs hidden).
4. If visible, try opening:
   ```
   /Android/data/com.whatsapp/
   ```
5. See if you can find your **Twin App's media folder**.

‚úÖ **Why this might work:** Some premium file managers (like X-Folder) have deeper access.

---

### **Option 2: Use ADB (For Full Access, Requires a PC)**
If Android won‚Äôt let you navigate there normally, we can **force access** using **ADB (Android Debug Bridge)**.

1. **Enable Developer Options**:
   - Go to **Settings > About Phone**.
   - Tap **Build Number** **7 times** until it says **"You are now a developer!"**.
   - Go to **Developer Options** and enable **USB Debugging**.

2. **Connect Your Phone to a PC** via USB.

3. **Run ADB Commands on Your PC**:
   - Install **Minimal ADB & Fastboot** (or ADB tools from Google).
   - Open **Command Prompt (Windows) or Terminal (Mac/Linux)**.
   - Run:
     ```
     adb devices
     ```
     (If your phone appears, ADB is working.)
   - Then, run:
     ```
     adb shell
     ```
     ```
     cd /storage/emulated/128/WhatsApp/Media/
     ```
     ```
     mv WhatsAppVoda\ Images /storage/emulated/0/WhatsApp/Media/
     ```
   - This moves the folder to your main WhatsApp storage.

‚úÖ **Why this works:** ADB bypasses Android's restrictions and lets you manually move files.

---

### **Option 3: Try Rooting (Not Ideal)**
- If you're comfortable, rooting the phone **removes all storage restrictions**.
- But it **voids your warranty and risks bricking your phone**.

---

### **Best Option for You?**
- **If X-Folder shows "Android/Data"** ‚Üí Try navigating inside.
- **If not, ADB is the best way to force access** (I can guide you through it).
- **If you‚Äôre not comfortable with ADB**, we can try a different workaround.

**Let me know how far you get, and I‚Äôll guide you from there!**
